  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>I propose to add several new methods to the ComplexUtils class enabling easy conversion between Complex[] arrays, real or imaginary double[] or float[] arrays, and interleaved complex double[] or float[] arrays. The last two in particular are beneficial to have for OpenCL implementations and the JTransforms library.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI think I would proceed in the following manner assuming we\'re trying to merge Eric\'s \u003ctt\u003efeature-\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/MATH-1290\\\" title=\\\"Additions to Complex Utils; creation of conversion methods between Complex[], double[], float[], and interleaved arrays\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"MATH-1290\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eMATH-1290\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/tt\u003e into the main apache commons-math \u003ctt\u003edevelop\u003c\\/tt\u003e branch (or master either should work). From a clean directory on Gilles\' machine I would run the following:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit clone git:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\\n\u003c\\/span\u003ecd commons-math\\ngit remote add ericbarnhill https:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\n\u003c\\/span\u003egit fetch --all\\ngit checkout -b feature-MATH-1290 ericbarnhill\\/feature-MATH-1290\\n&lt;&lt;Make and commit any needed changes to the branch here&gt;&gt;\\ngit checkout -b develop origin\\/develop\\ngit merge feature-MATH-1290\\n&lt;&lt;This should open vi and allow a commit message&gt;&gt;\\ngit push origin develop\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eThe explanation of the mechanics at play here follows below. Pardon my long-windedness. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003chr \\/\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eIt looks like to me that what we\'re trying to do here is get Eric\'s branch \u003ctt\u003efeature-\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/MATH-1290\\\" title=\\\"Additions to Complex Utils; creation of conversion methods between Complex[], double[], float[], and interleaved arrays\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"MATH-1290\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eMATH-1290\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/tt\u003e merged into the main repository\'s either \u003ctt\u003emaster\u003c\\/tt\u003e or \u003ctt\u003edevelop\u003c\\/tt\u003e branch. At a quick glance, it appears that either are reasonable choices, but for the exercise we only need one, so let\'s choose \u003ctt\u003edevelop\u003c\\/tt\u003e.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor the sake of discussion here, let\'s refer to Eric\'s repository \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/tt\u003e as \u003ctt\u003eericbarnhill\u003c\\/tt\u003e and the apache repository \u003ctt\u003egit:\\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\u003c\\/tt\u003e, to which Gilles makes his commits, as \u003ctt\u003eupstream\u003c\\/tt\u003e. Before going any further, we\'ll do a quick overview on the way git (unlike subversion) can handle working with a collection of repositories that are remote to one\'s machine. When we run the command:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit clone git:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003ewhat happens is two fold: (1) git copies the whole repository to your machine, and (2) git creates a named reference of the location from which you copied the repository, the default name here is \\\"origin.\\\" Now, once working from the directory into which git copied the files, presumably based on the command above, \u003ctt\u003e.\\/commons-math\u003c\\/tt\u003e we can add more repositories that we wish to use for collaboration each of which we can give a name. Let\'s take my current local setup as an  example, and consider the following commands run in succession, knowing the my copy of commons-math exists in the location \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/chtompki\\/commons-math.git\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/chtompki\\/commons-math.git\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit clone https:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/github.com\\/chtompki\\/commons-math.git\\n\u003c\\/span\u003ecd .\\/commons-math\\ngit remote add upstream git:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\\n\u003c\\/span\u003egit remote add ericbarnhill https:\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\n\u003c\\/span\u003egit fetch --all\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eWhat happens here is creates my repo locally, with it linked by default with my github \\\"chtompki\\\" location. I then add other repositories from which I want to work, namely \u003ctt\u003eericbarnhill\u003c\\/tt\u003e the name we\'ve given Eric\'s repository, and \u003ctt\u003eupstream\u003c\\/tt\u003e the name we\'ve given the main apache commons-math repo. Lastly, I\'ve run the fetch command to get all of the branches from each of the respective repositories.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNow, we have quite the collection of branches. If we run the git list branches command\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit branch -a\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003ewe see a host of repeated branches. We should see most of our branches listed in the form \u003ctt\u003eremotes\\/&lt;name-we-gave-our-remote&gt;\\/branch-name\u003c\\/tt\u003e. For example we should see the following occur some where in our list\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003eremotes\\/origin\\/master\\nremotes\\/upstream\\/master\\nremotes\\/ericbarnhill\\/master\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eeach of which represents the state of that branch in each location. Now to move onto one of these branches, all we need run is:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit checkout ericbarnhill\\/master\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eand that puts us on the master branch of Eric\'s repository with the state that it was in when we ran the \u003ctt\u003egit fetch --all\u003c\\/tt\u003e command, but because it\'s a remote reference, git will not let us commit to that branch. Thus we might want to create a working branch from the remote branch, which we could do in the following manner:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003egit checkout -b &lt;branch-name-of-our-choosing&gt; ericbarnhill\\/master\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eNow we are on a working copy of Eric\'s \u003ctt\u003emaster\u003c\\/tt\u003e branch and can work from there.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"chtompki\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15233313_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=chtompki\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"chtompki\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Rob Tompkins\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15233313_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Apr\\/16 02:55\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-04-09T02:55:28+0000\'\u003e09\\/Apr\\/16 02:55\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I think I would proceed in the following manner assuming we\'re trying to merge Eric\'s  feature-  MATH-1290    into the main apache commons-math  develop  branch (or master either should work). From a clean directory on Gilles\' machine I would run the following: \\n  \\n git clone git: \\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\\n cd commons-math\\ngit remote add ericbarnhill https: \\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\n git fetch --all\\ngit checkout -b feature-MATH-1290 ericbarnhill\\/feature-MATH-1290\\n&lt;&lt;Make and commit any needed changes to the branch here&gt;&gt;\\ngit checkout -b develop origin\\/develop\\ngit merge feature-MATH-1290\\n&lt;&lt;This should open vi and allow a commit message&gt;&gt;\\ngit push origin develop\\n \\n  \\n The explanation of the mechanics at play here follows below. Pardon my long-windedness.  \\n \\n It looks like to me that what we\'re trying to do here is get Eric\'s branch  feature-  MATH-1290    merged into the main repository\'s either  master  or  develop  branch. At a quick glance, it appears that either are reasonable choices, but for the exercise we only need one, so let\'s choose  develop . \\n\\n For the sake of discussion here, let\'s refer to Eric\'s repository   https:\\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git   as  ericbarnhill  and the apache repository  git:\\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git , to which Gilles makes his commits, as  upstream . Before going any further, we\'ll do a quick overview on the way git (unlike subversion) can handle working with a collection of repositories that are remote to one\'s machine. When we run the command: \\n\\n  \\n git clone git: \\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git \\n \\n  \\n what happens is two fold: (1) git copies the whole repository to your machine, and (2) git creates a named reference of the location from which you copied the repository, the default name here is \\\"origin.\\\" Now, once working from the directory into which git copied the files, presumably based on the command above,  .\\/commons-math  we can add more repositories that we wish to use for collaboration each of which we can give a name. Let\'s take my current local setup as an  example, and consider the following commands run in succession, knowing the my copy of commons-math exists in the location   https:\\/\\/github.com\\/chtompki\\/commons-math.git   \\n  \\n git clone https: \\/\\/github.com\\/chtompki\\/commons-math.git\\n cd .\\/commons-math\\ngit remote add upstream git: \\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\\n git remote add ericbarnhill https: \\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\n git fetch --all\\n \\n  \\n What happens here is creates my repo locally, with it linked by default with my github \\\"chtompki\\\" location. I then add other repositories from which I want to work, namely  ericbarnhill  the name we\'ve given Eric\'s repository, and  upstream  the name we\'ve given the main apache commons-math repo. Lastly, I\'ve run the fetch command to get all of the branches from each of the respective repositories. \\n\\n Now, we have quite the collection of branches. If we run the git list branches command \\n  \\n git branch -a\\n \\n  \\n we see a host of repeated branches. We should see most of our branches listed in the form  remotes\\/&lt;name-we-gave-our-remote&gt;\\/branch-name . For example we should see the following occur some where in our list \\n  \\n remotes\\/origin\\/master\\nremotes\\/upstream\\/master\\nremotes\\/ericbarnhill\\/master\\n \\n  \\n each of which represents the state of that branch in each location. Now to move onto one of these branches, all we need run is: \\n  \\n git checkout ericbarnhill\\/master\\n \\n  \\n and that puts us on the master branch of Eric\'s repository with the state that it was in when we ran the  git fetch --all  command, but because it\'s a remote reference, git will not let us commit to that branch. Thus we might want to create a working branch from the remote branch, which we could do in the following manner: \\n  \\n git checkout -b &lt;branch-name-of-our-choosing&gt; ericbarnhill\\/master\\n \\n  \\n Now we are on a working copy of Eric\'s  master  branch and can work from there.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n      I see Gilles, you are looking for the least invasive procedure to merge the changes in. Before I go into how to do the merge in the least invasive way possible, let me give a brief description of my understanding of the mechanics beind \\\"git\'s\\\"  pull  command. I think it\'s fundamentally a  git fetch  followed by a  git merge . For this to happen we still need a reference to the remote repository in question as well as the individual branch in question. That said, I would perform the following steps again assuming that the branch to which we wish to merge is named develop (but it need not be): \\n  \\n git clone git: \\/\\/git.apache.org\\/commons-math.git\\n cd commons-math\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt;have done standard work and now want to merge in the pull request from a branch named feature-MATH-1290&gt;&gt;\\n git remote add ericbarnhill https: \\/\\/github.com\\/ericbarnhill\\/commons-math.git\\n git fetch ericbarnhill feature-MATH-1290\\n \\/\\/&lt; this  creates a single  new  remote branch reference, namely remotes\\/ericbarnhill\\/feature-MATH-1290&gt;&gt;\\n  \\/\\/&lt;&lt;I would still want a local copy  for  the sake of making changes so the below still applies&gt;&gt;\\n git checkout -b feature-MATH-1290 ericbarnhill\\/feature-MATH-1290\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt;Make and commit any needed changes to the branch here&gt;&gt;\\n git checkout -b develop origin\\/develop\\ngit merge feature-MATH-1290\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt;This should open vi and allow a commit message&gt;&gt;\\n git push origin develop\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt;now suppose I want to remove all references to Eric\'s repository, I would perform the following&gt;&gt;\\n git branch -D feature-MATH-1290\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt; this  deletes my local copy of the fetched remote reference branch&gt;&gt;\\n git remote rm ericbarnhill\\n \\/\\/&lt;&lt; this  deletes my remote reference to Eric\'s repository, leaving me back in my previous state only with feature-MATH-1290 now merged in&gt;&gt; \\n \\n  \\n\\n GitHub has the mechanics in place in it\'s online user interface to do a pull request with a click of a button, but I think under the hood it performs the exact commands above or if not something extremely similar.
